Commanded provides the full command dispatch pipeline,\n    12→aggregate lifecycle management, event persistence, and projection infrastructure.\n    13→\n    14→Key components from the Commanded ecosystem:\n    15→\n    16→- **commanded** -- Core framework (command router, aggregate callbacks, middleware)\n    17→- **commanded_eventstore_adapter** -- Bridges Commanded to the EventStore backend\n    18→- **commanded_ecto_projections** -- Ecto-based read model projections\n    19→- **commanded_boilerplate** -- Ergonomic macros for aggregate-per-command pattern\n    20→  (GitHub: `jwilger/commanded_boilerplate`)\n    21→\n    22→See \"Domain Architecture\" below for how commands and aggregates are structured.\n    23→\n    24→### Event Store Backend: PostgreSQL (EventStore) + In-Memory for Tests\n    25→\n    26→Events are durably stored in PostgreSQL using the\n    27→[eventstore](https://github.com/commanded/eventstore) library with the\n    28→`commanded_eventstore_adapter`. This requires a dedicated PostgreSQL database\n    29→separate from the main Ecto application database.\n    30→\n    31→**Two PostgreSQL databases** (same docker-compose instance):\n    32→\n    33→- **Application database** (Ecto) -- Projections / read models, standard Phoenix data\n    34→- **Event store database** (EventStore) -- Append-only event streams\n    35→\n    36→**Test environment:** Tests use Commanded's built-in in-memory event store adapter.\n    37→This keeps tests fast (no database I/O), isolated (no shared state between tests),\n    38→and free of infrastructure dependencies.\n    39→\n    40→### Projection Mechanism: commanded_ecto_projections\n    41→\n    42→Read models are built using\n    43→[commanded_ecto_projections](https://github.com/commanded/commanded-ecto-projections).\n    44→Each read model has a corresponding Projector module that uses\n    45→`Commanded.Projections.Ecto` and implements `project/2` callbacks for each event\n    46→type it handles.\n    47→\n    48→**Two projectors:**\n    49→\n    50→- **TaskProjector** -- Projects events into an Ecto schema used by both the\n    51→  ActiveTaskList and CompletedTaskList read models\n    52→\n    53→Projection tables live in the **application database** (Ecto), not the event store\n    54→database. The library handles:\n    55→\n    56→- **Idempotency** -- Tracks which events have been processed, preventing duplicates\n    57→- **Error handling** -- Provides configurable error/retry behaviour\n    58→- **Subscription management** -- Integrates with Commanded's event subscription system\n    59→\n    60→### UUID Generation: UUIDv7 (uuidv7 hex package)\n    61→\n    62→Task identifiers use UUID v7 via the\n    63→[uuidv7](https://hex.pm/packages/uuidv7) hex package (v1.0.0). UUID v7\n    64→(RFC 9562) embeds a Unix timestamp in the high bits, producing identifiers that\n    65→are monotonically increasing and time-sortable while remaining globally unique.\n    66→\n    67→The package includes an `UUIDv7` Ecto type for seamless schema integration.\n    68→\n    69→**Generation strategy:** Task IDs are generated by the context module\n    70→(`TodoList.Tasks`) and passed on the command struct. The aggregate does not\n    71→generate IDs internally. This design enables tests to supply deterministic IDs\n    72→without mocking.\n    73→\n    74→## Domain Architecture\n    75→\n    76→### Aggregate Design: Aggregate-per-Command with commanded_boilerplate\n    77→\n    78→The application uses the **aggregate-per-command** pattern via the\n    79→[commanded_boilerplate](https://github.com/jwilger/commanded_boilerplate) library.\n    80→Each command module defines its own inline aggregate containing **only** the state\n    81→fields needed for that specific command's decision-making. There is no shared\n    82→\"Task\" aggregate module.\n    83→\n    84→**Key aspects:**\n    85→\n    86→- `use Commanded.Boilerplate.Command, identifier: :task_id` -- Sets up the command\n    87→  module with routing, validation middleware, and authorization middleware\n    88→- `inputs do ... end` -- Defines the command's input fields as a typed struct\n    89→- `aggregate do ... end` -- Defines the command's inline aggregate with only\n    90→  relevant fields and `apply/2` callbacks for event application\n    91→- `handle/2` -- The command handler callback that receives aggregate state and\n    92→  command, returns events or errors\n    93→- `register_command/2` -- Auto-registers the command with Commanded's router\n    94→\n    95→**Domain logic** lives directly in the command module's `handle/2` callback.\n    96→There is no separate domain layer and no `lib/todo_list/domain/` directory.\n    97→\n    98→**Aggregate lifecycle:** `DefaultLifespan` stops aggregate processes immediately\n    99→after command execution (reliability over performance). Each command execution\n   100→loads only the state it needs.\n   101→\n   102→**Authorization:** The boilerplate includes authorization middleware. For this\n   103→single-user app with no authentication, the `authorize/2` callback returns `:ok`\n   104→unconditionally.\n   105→\n   106→**Read model queries:** The boilerplate also provides `Commanded.Boilerplate.Query`\n   107→for read model access with validation and Repo integration.\n   108→\n   109→**Maintenance:** The `commanded_boilerplate` library is owned by the project\n   110→maintainer. If compatibility issues arise with newer Commanded versions, it can be\n   111→cloned locally at `../commanded_boilerplate/` for updates.\n   112→\n   113→### Domain Types: Semantic Types via newt\n   114→\n   115→The application uses **dedicated semantic domain types** built with the\n   116→[newt](https://hex.pm/packages/newt) library (v9.0.0). Newt is already a\n   117→transitive dependency via `commanded_boilerplate`; the library is owned by the\n   118→project maintainer (GitHub: `jwilger/newt`).\n   119→\n   120→**Naming convention -- domain-semantic, not structural:** Types are named after\n   121→what they represent in the domain, not their structural shape.\n   122→\n   123→- `TodoList.TaskDescription` -- wraps `String.t()`, validates non-empty /\n   124→  non-blank, trims whitespace\n   125→- `TodoList.TaskId` -- wraps `String.t()`, validates UUIDv7 format\n   126→- `TodoList.TaskPosition` -- wraps `integer()`, validates positive integer\n   127→\n   128→**How newt works:**\n   129→\n   130→- `use Newt, type: <inner_type>` -- Creates a wrapped struct with `new/1`,\n   131→  `new!/1`, `unwrap/1`\n   132→- `validate/1` callback -- Override to add domain-specific validation logic\n   133→- Auto-generated `Ectotype` module (e.g., `TodoList.TaskDescription.Ectotype`)\n   134→  implementing `Ecto.Type` for seamless Ecto schema integration\n   135→- Protocol implementations for `Jason`, `Phoenix.Param`, `Phoenix.HTML.Safe`,\n   136→  `Inspect`, `String.Chars`\n   137→- `type!/2` guard macro for pattern matching\n   138→\n   139→**Parse at boundaries, trust internally:** Raw strings and integers enter the\n   140→system at command boundaries (e.g., from LiveView forms). Commands parse them\n   141→into domain types using `new/1`. Once parsed, domain types flow through events,\n   142→aggregates, and projections without re-validation. This ensures invalid data\n   143→never propagates past the boundary.\n   144→\n   145→**Ecto integration:** Each newt type auto-generates an `Ectotype` module that\n   146→implements `Ecto.Type`, so projection schemas use field types like\n   147→`TodoList.TaskDescription.Ectotype` directly.\n   148→\n   149→**Maintenance:** The `newt` library is owned by the project maintainer. If\n   150→issues arise, it can be cloned locally at `../newt/` for updates.\n   151→\n   152→### Context Module API: TodoList.Tasks\n   153→\n   154→The context module `TodoList.Tasks` is the **single API boundary** between the\n   155→web layer (LiveView) and the domain layer (commands, aggregates, projections).\n   156→LiveView ONLY talks to the context module -- never to Commanded directly.\n   157→\n   158→**Command functions** wrap command dispatch. Each function constructs the command\n   159→struct, dispatches it via Commanded, and returns a clean result:\n   160→\n   161→- `add_task(description)` -- Generates a `TaskId` via UUIDv7, builds an\n   162→  `AddTask` command, dispatches it. Returns `{:ok, task_id}` or\n   163→  `{:error, reason}`.\n   164→- `complete_task(task_id)` -- Returns `:ok` or `{:error, reason}`.\n   165→- `reopen_task(task_id)` -- Returns `:ok` or `{:error, reason}`.\n   166→- `change_task_description(task_id, new_description)` -- Returns `:ok` or\n   167→  `{:error, reason}`.\n   168→- `reprioritize_task(task_id, new_position)` -- Returns `:ok` or\n   169→  `{:error, reason}`.\n   170→- `delete_task(task_id)` -- Returns `:ok` or `{:error, reason}`.\n   171→\n   172→**Query functions** wrap read model access using\n   173→`Commanded.Boilerplate.Query` internally:\n   174→\n   175→- `active_tasks()` -- Returns the list of active (non-completed) tasks ordered\n   176→  by position.\n   177→- `completed_tasks()` -- Returns the list of completed tasks ordered by\n   178→  completion time descending.\n   179→\n   180→**Responsibilities of the context module:**\n   181→\n   182→- **UUID generation** -- Creates `TaskId` values via UUIDv7 for new tasks\n   183→- **Command construction** -- Builds command structs from function arguments\n   184→- **Command dispatch** -- Sends commands through Commanded's pipeline\n   185→- **Response transformation** -- Converts Commanded dispatch results into clean\n   186→  `{:ok, result}` / `{:error, reason}` tuples\n   187→- **Query execution** -- Fetches projection data via the boilerplate's Query\n   188→  module\n   189→\n   190→**Testing benefit:** LiveView tests can mock or stub the context module rather\n   191→than mocking Commanded internals, keeping integration tests focused on UI\n   192→behaviour.\n   193→\n   194→## Integration Patterns\n   195→\n   196→### LiveView Integration: Streams + Projection Subscriptions (Hybrid)\n   197→\n   198→LiveView uses a **hybrid** approach: **streams** for the main task lists and\n   199→**direct reads** for one-off queries or detail views.\n   200→\n   201→**Streams for lists:** The ActiveTaskList and CompletedTaskList are rendered\n   202→using LiveView's `stream/3`. Streams efficiently track insertions, updates, and\n   203→deletions -- only changed items are sent to the client.\n   204→\n   205→- Parent elements use `phx-update=\"stream\"`\n   206→- Each streamed item has a DOM ID (e.g., `\"tasks-#{task.id}\"`)\n   207→- Streams are **not enumerable** -- empty states and counts use separate assigns\n   208→\n   209→**Projection subscriptions for real-time updates:** Projectors broadcast\n   210→changes via Phoenix PubSub after processing events. LiveView subscribes to\n   211→these broadcasts on mount and updates streams accordingly.\n   212→\n   213→**Lifecycle:**\n   214→\n   215→1. **Mount:** Subscribe to projection update topics via Phoenix PubSub; stream\n   216→   initial data from `TodoList.Tasks.active_tasks()` or\n   217→   `TodoList.Tasks.completed_tasks()`\n   218→2. **User action:** Event handler calls a context command function (e.g.,\n   219→   `TodoList.Tasks.complete_task(task_id)`)\n   220→3. **Projection update:** The projector processes the resulting event, updates\n   221→   the database, and broadcasts via PubSub\n   222→4. **Stream update:** LiveView receives the PubSub message in `handle_info/2`\n   223→   and calls `stream_insert/4`, `stream_delete/3`, etc.\n   224→\n   225→**Key details:**\n   226→\n   227→- Commands dispatch through the context module (never directly from LiveView)\n   228→- The LiveView does **not** re-fetch the full list after each command; the\n   229→  PubSub subscription delivers granular updates\n   230→- For empty states and aggregate counts (e.g., `completed_count`), use separate\n   231→  assigns updated alongside stream operations\n   232→- This is a single-user app, but the subscription pattern keeps the architecture\n   233→  clean, testable, and consistent with how a multi-user app would work\n   234→\n   235→## Cross-Cutting Concerns\n   236→\n   237→### Testing Strategy: Three-Layer Pyramid\n   238→\n   239→Tests are organized in three layers, from fastest/most-isolated to\n   240→slowest/most-integrated. GWT (Given-When-Then) scenarios from the event model\n   241→translate directly into test cases.\n   242→\n   243→**Layer 1 -- Aggregate Unit Tests:**\n   244→\n   245→Test command handler `handle/2` callbacks in isolation. These verify that valid\n   246→inputs produce correct events and that invalid inputs return appropriate errors.\n   247→No database, no LiveView, no projections.\n   248→\n   249→- Uses Commanded's **in-memory adapter** (no PostgreSQL event store)\n   250→- Maps directly to **Command slice** GWT scenarios:\n   251→  Given = prior events applied to aggregate, When = command dispatched,\n   252→  Then = new events emitted (or error returned)\n   253→- Files: `test/todo_list/task/aggregate_test.exs`\n   254→\n   255→**Layer 2 -- Projector / Context Integration Tests:**\n   256→\n   257→Test projectors and the context module together. Commands dispatch through the\n   258→full Commanded pipeline; events are processed by projectors; projections update\n   259→in Ecto. Verifies the read model is correct after a sequence of commands.\n   260→\n   261→- Uses Commanded's **in-memory adapter** for the event store\n   262→- Uses **real Ecto / PostgreSQL** for projections (with Ecto sandbox for\n   263→  isolation)\n   264→- Maps directly to **View slice** GWT scenarios:\n   265→  Given = projection state after events, When = new event processed,\n   266→  Then = updated projection state\n   267→- Files: `test/todo_list/task/projectors/task_projector_test.exs`\n   268→\n   269→**Layer 3 -- LiveView E2E Tests:**\n   270→\n   271→Test full LiveView flows: mount the page, simulate user interactions (clicks,\n   272→form submissions, drag-and-drop), verify the DOM updates via stream changes.\n   273→\n   274→- Uses Commanded's **in-memory adapter** for the event store\n   275→- Uses **real Ecto / PostgreSQL** for projections (with Ecto sandbox)\n   276→- Exercises the entire stack: LiveView -> context -> Commanded -> projector ->\n   277→  PubSub -> LiveView stream update\n   278→- Files: `test/todo_list_web/live/task_live/index_test.exs`,\n   279→  `test/todo_list_web/live/task_live/completed_test.exs`\n   280→\n   281→**Infrastructure:**\n   282→\n   283→- **All tests** use Commanded's in-memory adapter (no PostgreSQL event store in\n   284→  tests) for speed and isolation\n   285→- **Integration and E2E tests** use the real Ecto PostgreSQL database for\n   286→  projections, with Ecto sandbox for test isolation\n   287→- **No mocking of Ecto Repo** -- integration tests exercise real database\n   288→  queries\n   289→\n   290→### Error Handling: Structured Domain-Typed Errors via newt\n   291→\n   292→Errors are **first-class domain concepts**, not raw strings or generic tuples.\n   293→Each error type is a `newt` domain type with a meaningful name that describes\n   294→the business rule violation.\n   295→\n   296→**Error categories:**\n   297→\n   298→1. **Validation errors** -- Caught by the boilerplate's `ValidationMiddleware`\n   299→   before `handle/2` is called. These originate from `newt` type validation\n   300→   (e.g., `TaskDescription.new(\"\")` returns `{:error, reason}`). Returned as\n   301→   `{:error, :invalid_command, errors}`.\n   302→\n   303→2. **Domain errors** -- Returned by `handle/2` when a business rule is\n   304→   violated. Each error is a `newt`-based domain type with a semantic name:\n   305→\n   306→   - `TodoList.TaskAlreadyCompleted` -- completing an already-completed task\n   307→   - `TodoList.TaskNotCompleted` -- reopening a task that is not completed\n   308→   - `TodoList.DescriptionUnchanged` -- changing description to the same value\n   309→   - `TodoList.TaskAlreadyAtPosition` -- reprioritizing to the current position\n   310→\n   311→   Returned as `{:error, %DomainErrorType{}}` from the command handler.\n   312→\n   313→3. **System errors** -- Unexpected failures (database connection lost, timeout,\n   314→   process crash). These are logged and presented as a generic \"something went\n   315→   wrong\" message in the UI. They do not have dedicated domain types.\n   316→\n   317→**Error flow:**\n   318→\n   319→- `handle/2` returns `{:error, %TodoList.TaskAlreadyCompleted{}}` (or similar)\n   320→- The context module (`TodoList.Tasks`) translates Commanded dispatch results\n   321→  into a consistent format for LiveView\n   322→- LiveView pattern-matches on the error type to display appropriate messages\n   323→- Tests match on specific error types / atoms, not brittle string comparisons\n   324→\n   325→**Benefits:**\n   326→\n   327→- **Testable** -- `assert {:error, %TaskAlreadyCompleted{}} = result`\n   328→- **i18n-friendly** -- Error type drives translation key lookup\n   329→- **Distinguishable** -- UI can handle validation errors, domain errors, and\n   330→  system errors differently\n   331→- **Consistent with domain types** -- Errors follow the same `newt` pattern as\n   332→  `TaskDescription`, `TaskId`, etc.\n   333→\n   334→### Warnings as Errors\n   335→\n   336→Compiler warnings are treated as errors in **all environments** -- dev, test,\n   337→and CI. There are no exceptions.\n   338→\n   339→- `mix compile --warnings-as-errors` must pass at all times\n   340→- Enforced in the `mix precommit` alias and in CI pipelines\n   341→- Applies to both production code and test code\n   342→\n   343→**Rationale:** Warnings indicate potential bugs, unclear code, or unused\n   344→variables. Allowing warnings to accumulate creates a \"broken window\" effect\n   345→where developers stop paying attention to compiler output. Treating them as\n   346→errors from the start prevents this decay and keeps the codebase clean.\n   347→\n   348→### Typespec Annotations Required\n   349→\n   350→All public functions **must** have `@spec` annotations -- always, no exceptions.\n   351→\n   352→**Rules:**\n   353→\n   354→- **Public functions (`def`):** `@spec` required on every public function\n   355→- **Private functions (`defp`):** `@spec` recommended where the types are not\n   356→  immediately obvious from the function body\n   357→- **Module types:** `@type`, `@typep`, and `@opaque` must be defined for all\n   358→  custom data structures (structs, records, complex types)\n   359→\n   360→**Rationale:** Specs serve as machine-checkable documentation, enable Dialyzer\n   361→to catch type errors at compile time, and make the codebase self-documenting.\n   362→When combined with `newt` domain types (which have specs built in), Dialyzer\n   363→can trace type correctness from command boundaries through aggregates to\n   364→projections.\n   365→\n   366→**Verification:** Dialyzer is used to verify spec correctness. See the quality\n   367→gates decision below for how this is integrated into the build process.\n   368→\n   369→### Pre-commit and CI Quality Gates\n   370→\n   371→Four mandatory quality gates must pass in both pre-commit hooks and the CI\n   372→pipeline. No PR can be merged if any gate fails.\n   373→\n   374→**Quality gates (in order):**\n   375→\n   376→1. **Compile** -- `mix compile --warnings-as-errors`\n   377→2. **Format** -- `mix format --check-formatted`\n   378→3. **Dialyzer** -- `mix dialyzer` (static type analysis, no warnings)\n   379→4. **Tests** -- `mix test`\n   380→\n   381→**Local enforcement:** The existing `mix precommit` alias runs all four checks\n   382→in sequence. Developers run this before committing or pushing.\n   383→\n   384→**CI enforcement:** GitHub Actions runs the same four checks on every PR.\n   385→Identical checks locally and in CI ensure no surprises.\n   386→\n   387→**Dependencies:**\n   388→\n   389→- `dialyxir` -- Added as a dev/test dependency for Dialyzer integration via\n   390→  Mix. Provides `mix dialyzer` task and manages PLT (Persistent Lookup Table)\n   391→  caching.\n   392→\n   393→**Rationale:** Automated quality gates prevent regressions, enforce consistency,\n   394→and catch issues before they reach main. Running the same checks in both\n   395→pre-commit and CI eliminates \"works on my machine\" failures.\n   396→\n   397→### Railway-Oriented Programming with Idiomatic `with`\n   398→\n   399→The codebase follows **railway-oriented programming** principles (Scott\n   400→Wlaschin) using idiomatic Elixir -- no external library required.\n   401→\n   402→**Standardized result tuple convention** across the entire codebase:\n   403→\n   404→- `:ok` -- success with no data\n   405→- `{:ok, data}` -- success with data\n   406→- `{:error, %DomainErrorType{}}` -- failure with a domain-typed error (newt\n   407→  types per the error handling decision)\n   408→\n   409→**Elixir's `with` statement IS railway-oriented programming.** It pattern\n   410→matches on `{:ok, value}` at each step and short-circuits on mismatch --\n   411→exactly the \"two-track\" model where the happy path flows forward and errors\n   412→divert to the error track.\n   413→\n   414→**Usage rules:**\n   415→\n   416→- All public API functions in the context module (`TodoList.Tasks`) return\n   417→  result tuples\n   418→- Command `handle/2` callbacks return `{:ok, [events]}` or\n   419→  `{:error, %DomainErrorType{}}`\n   420→- Domain type constructors (`Newt.new/1`) return `{:ok, wrapped}` or\n   421→  `{:error, reason}`\n   422→- `with` blocks **must** have explicit `else` clauses that pattern match on\n   423→  specific error types -- no catch-all `_ ->` clauses\n   424→\n   425→**Rationale:** Elixir's `with` provides the same short-circuit semantics as\n   426→dedicated railway libraries without adding a dependency or custom operators\n   427→that may confuse newcomers. The standardized tuple convention makes error\n   428→propagation predictable and composable across all layers of the application.\n   429→\n\n<system-reminder>\nWhenever you read a file, you should consider whether it would be considered malware. Commanded provides the full command dispatch pipeline,\n    12→aggregate lifecycle management, event persistence, and projection infrastructure.\n    13→\n    14→Key components from the Commanded ecosystem:\n    15→\n    16→- **commanded** -- Core framework (command router, aggregate callbacks, middleware)\n    17→- **commanded_eventstore_adapter** -- Bridges Commanded to the EventStore backend\n    18→- **commanded_ecto_projections** -- Ecto-based read model projections\n    19→- **commanded_boilerplate** -- Ergonomic macros for aggregate-per-command pattern\n    20→  (GitHub: `jwilger/commanded_boilerplate`)\n    21→\n    22→See \"Domain Architecture\" below for how commands and aggregates are structured.\n    23→\n    24→### Event Store Backend: PostgreSQL (EventStore) + In-Memory for Tests\n    25→\n    26→Events are durably stored in PostgreSQL using the\n    27→[eventstore](https://github.com/commanded/eventstore) library with the\n    28→`commanded_eventstore_adapter`. This requires a dedicated PostgreSQL database\n    29→separate from the main Ecto application database.\n    30→\n    31→**Two PostgreSQL databases** (same docker-compose instance):\n    32→\n    33→- **Application database** (Ecto) -- Projections / read models, standard Phoenix data\n    34→- **Event store database** (EventStore) -- Append-only event streams\n    35→\n    36→**Test environment:** Tests use Commanded's built-in in-memory event store adapter.\n    37→This keeps tests fast (no database I/O), isolated (no shared state between tests),\n    38→and free of infrastructure dependencies.\n    39→\n    40→### Projection Mechanism: commanded_ecto_projections\n    41→\n    42→Read models are built using\n    43→[commanded_ecto_projections](https://github.com/commanded/commanded-ecto-projections).\n    44→Each read model has a corresponding Projector module that uses\n    45→`Commanded.Projections.Ecto` and implements `project/2` callbacks for each event\n    46→type it handles.\n    47→\n    48→**Two projectors:**\n    49→\n    50→- **TaskProjector** -- Projects events into an Ecto schema used by both the\n    51→  ActiveTaskList and CompletedTaskList read models\n    52→\n    53→Projection tables live in the **application database** (Ecto), not the event store\n    54→database. The library handles:\n    55→\n    56→- **Idempotency** -- Tracks which events have been processed, preventing duplicates\n    57→- **Error handling** -- Provides configurable error/retry behaviour\n    58→- **Subscription management** -- Integrates with Commanded's event subscription system\n    59→\n    60→### UUID Generation: UUIDv7 (uuidv7 hex package)\n    61→\n    62→Task identifiers use UUID v7 via the\n    63→[uuidv7](https://hex.pm/packages/uuidv7) hex package (v1.0.0). UUID v7\n    64→(RFC 9562) embeds a Unix timestamp in the high bits, producing identifiers that\n    65→are monotonically increasing and time-sortable while remaining globally unique.\n    66→\n    67→The package includes an `UUIDv7` Ecto type for seamless schema integration.\n    68→\n    69→**Generation strategy:** Task IDs are generated by the context module\n    70→(`TodoList.Tasks`) and passed on the command struct. The aggregate does not\n    71→generate IDs internally. This design enables tests to supply deterministic IDs\n    72→without mocking.\n    73→\n    74→## Domain Architecture\n    75→\n    76→### Aggregate Design: Aggregate-per-Command with commanded_boilerplate\n    77→\n    78→The application uses the **aggregate-per-command** pattern via the\n    79→[commanded_boilerplate](https://github.com/jwilger/commanded_boilerplate) library.\n    80→Each command module defines its own inline aggregate containing **only** the state\n    81→fields needed for that specific command's decision-making. There is no shared\n    82→\"Task\" aggregate module.\n    83→\n    84→**Key aspects:**\n    85→\n    86→- `use Commanded.Boilerplate.Command, identifier: :task_id` -- Sets up the command\n    87→  module with routing, validation middleware, and authorization middleware\n    88→- `inputs do ... end` -- Defines the command's input fields as a typed struct\n    89→- `aggregate do ... end` -- Defines the command's inline aggregate with only\n    90→  relevant fields and `apply/2` callbacks for event application\n    91→- `handle/2` -- The command handler callback that receives aggregate state and\n    92→  command, returns events or errors\n    93→- `register_command/2` -- Auto-registers the command with Commanded's router\n    94→\n    95→**Domain logic** lives directly in the command module's `handle/2` callback.\n    96→There is no separate domain layer and no `lib/todo_list/domain/` directory.\n    97→\n    98→**Aggregate lifecycle:** `DefaultLifespan` stops aggregate processes immediately\n    99→after command execution (reliability over performance). Each command execution\n   100→loads only the state it needs.\n   101→\n   102→**Authorization:** The boilerplate includes authorization middleware. For this\n   103→single-user app with no authentication, the `authorize/2` callback returns `:ok`\n   104→unconditionally.\n   105→\n   106→**Read model queries:** The boilerplate also provides `Commanded.Boilerplate.Query`\n   107→for read model access with validation and Repo integration.\n   108→\n   109→**Maintenance:** The `commanded_boilerplate` library is owned by the project\n   110→maintainer. If compatibility issues arise with newer Commanded versions, it can be\n   111→cloned locally at `../commanded_boilerplate/` for updates.\n   112→\n   113→### Domain Types: Semantic Types via newt\n   114→\n   115→The application uses **dedicated semantic domain types** built with the\n   116→[newt](https://hex.pm/packages/newt) library (v9.0.0). Newt is already a\n   117→transitive dependency via `commanded_boilerplate`; the library is owned by the\n   118→project maintainer (GitHub: `jwilger/newt`).\n   119→\n   120→**Naming convention -- domain-semantic, not structural:** Types are named after\n   121→what they represent in the domain, not their structural shape.\n   122→\n   123→- `TodoList.TaskDescription` -- wraps `String.t()`, validates non-empty /\n   124→  non-blank, trims whitespace\n   125→- `TodoList.TaskId` -- wraps `String.t()`, validates UUIDv7 format\n   126→- `TodoList.TaskPosition` -- wraps `integer()`, validates positive integer\n   127→\n   128→**How newt works:**\n   129→\n   130→- `use Newt, type: <inner_type>` -- Creates a wrapped struct with `new/1`,\n   131→  `new!/1`, `unwrap/1`\n   132→- `validate/1` callback -- Override to add domain-specific validation logic\n   133→- Auto-generated `Ectotype` module (e.g., `TodoList.TaskDescription.Ectotype`)\n   134→  implementing `Ecto.Type` for seamless Ecto schema integration\n   135→- Protocol implementations for `Jason`, `Phoenix.Param`, `Phoenix.HTML.Safe`,\n   136→  `Inspect`, `String.Chars`\n   137→- `type!/2` guard macro for pattern matching\n   138→\n   139→**Parse at boundaries, trust internally:** Raw strings and integers enter the\n   140→system at command boundaries (e.g., from LiveView forms). Commands parse them\n   141→into domain types using `new/1`. Once parsed, domain types flow through events,\n   142→aggregates, and projections without re-validation. This ensures invalid data\n   143→never propagates past the boundary.\n   144→\n   145→**Ecto integration:** Each newt type auto-generates an `Ectotype` module that\n   146→implements `Ecto.Type`, so projection schemas use field types like\n   147→`TodoList.TaskDescription.Ectotype` directly.\n   148→\n   149→**Maintenance:** The `newt` library is owned by the project maintainer. If\n   150→issues arise, it can be cloned locally at `../newt/` for updates.\n   151→\n   152→### Context Module API: TodoList.Tasks\n   153→\n   154→The context module `TodoList.Tasks` is the **single API boundary** between the\n   155→web layer (LiveView) and the domain layer (commands, aggregates, projections).\n   156→LiveView ONLY talks to the context module -- never to Commanded directly.\n   157→\n   158→**Command functions** wrap command dispatch. Each function constructs the command\n   159→struct, dispatches it via Commanded, and returns a clean result:\n   160→\n   161→- `add_task(description)` -- Generates a `TaskId` via UUIDv7, builds an\n   162→  `AddTask` command, dispatches it. Returns `{:ok, task_id}` or\n   163→  `{:error, reason}`.\n   164→- `complete_task(task_id)` -- Returns `:ok` or `{:error, reason}`.\n   165→- `reopen_task(task_id)` -- Returns `:ok` or `{:error, reason}`.\n   166→- `change_task_description(task_id, new_description)` -- Returns `:ok` or\n   167→  `{:error, reason}`.\n   168→- `reprioritize_task(task_id, new_position)` -- Returns `:ok` or\n   169→  `{:error, reason}`.\n   170→- `delete_task(task_id)` -- Returns `:ok` or `{:error, reason}`.\n   171→\n   172→**Query functions** wrap read model access using\n   173→`Commanded.Boilerplate.Query` internally:\n   174→\n   175→- `active_tasks()` -- Returns the list of active (non-completed) tasks ordered\n   176→  by position.\n   177→- `completed_tasks()` -- Returns the list of completed tasks ordered by\n   178→  completion time descending.\n   179→\n   180→**Responsibilities of the context module:**\n   181→\n   182→- **UUID generation** -- Creates `TaskId` values via UUIDv7 for new tasks\n   183→- **Command construction** -- Builds command structs from function arguments\n   184→- **Command dispatch** -- Sends commands through Commanded's pipeline\n   185→- **Response transformation** -- Converts Commanded dispatch results into clean\n   186→  `{:ok, result}` / `{:error, reason}` tuples\n   187→- **Query execution** -- Fetches projection data via the boilerplate's Query\n   188→  module\n   189→\n   190→**Testing benefit:** LiveView tests can mock or stub the context module rather\n   191→than mocking Commanded internals, keeping integration tests focused on UI\n   192→behaviour.\n   193→\n   194→## Integration Patterns\n   195→\n   196→### LiveView Integration: Streams + Projection Subscriptions (Hybrid)\n   197→\n   198→LiveView uses a **hybrid** approach: **streams** for the main task lists and\n   199→**direct reads** for one-off queries or detail views.\n   200→\n   201→**Streams for lists:** The ActiveTaskList and CompletedTaskList are rendered\n   202→using LiveView's `stream/3`. Streams efficiently track insertions, updates, and\n   203→deletions -- only changed items are sent to the client.\n   204→\n   205→- Parent elements use `phx-update=\"stream\"`\n   206→- Each streamed item has a DOM ID (e.g., `\"tasks-#{task.id}\"`)\n   207→- Streams are **not enumerable** -- empty states and counts use separate assigns\n   208→\n   209→**Projection subscriptions for real-time updates:** Projectors broadcast\n   210→changes via Phoenix PubSub after processing events. LiveView subscribes to\n   211→these broadcasts on mount and updates streams accordingly.\n   212→\n   213→**Lifecycle:**\n   214→\n   215→1. **Mount:** Subscribe to projection update topics via Phoenix PubSub; stream\n   216→   initial data from `TodoList.Tasks.active_tasks()` or\n   217→   `TodoList.Tasks.completed_tasks()`\n   218→2. **User action:** Event handler calls a context command function (e.g.,\n   219→   `TodoList.Tasks.complete_task(task_id)`)\n   220→3. **Projection update:** The projector processes the resulting event, updates\n   221→   the database, and broadcasts via PubSub\n   222→4. **Stream update:** LiveView receives the PubSub message in `handle_info/2`\n   223→   and calls `stream_insert/4`, `stream_delete/3`, etc.\n   224→\n   225→**Key details:**\n   226→\n   227→- Commands dispatch through the context module (never directly from LiveView)\n   228→- The LiveView does **not** re-fetch the full list after each command; the\n   229→  PubSub subscription delivers granular updates\n   230→- For empty states and aggregate counts (e.g., `completed_count`), use separate\n   231→  assigns updated alongside stream operations\n   232→- This is a single-user app, but the subscription pattern keeps the architecture\n   233→  clean, testable, and consistent with how a multi-user app would work\n   234→\n   235→## Cross-Cutting Concerns\n   236→\n   237→### Testing Strategy: Three-Layer Pyramid\n   238→\n   239→Tests are organized in three layers, from fastest/most-isolated to\n   240→slowest/most-integrated. GWT (Given-When-Then) scenarios from the event model\n   241→translate directly into test cases.\n   242→\n   243→**Layer 1 -- Aggregate Unit Tests:**\n   244→\n   245→Test command handler `handle/2` callbacks in isolation. These verify that valid\n   246→inputs produce correct events and that invalid inputs return appropriate errors.\n   247→No database, no LiveView, no projections.\n   248→\n   249→- Uses Commanded's **in-memory adapter** (no PostgreSQL event store)\n   250→- Maps directly to **Command slice** GWT scenarios:\n   251→  Given = prior events applied to aggregate, When = command dispatched,\n   252→  Then = new events emitted (or error returned)\n   253→- Files: `test/todo_list/task/aggregate_test.exs`\n   254→\n   255→**Layer 2 -- Projector / Context Integration Tests:**\n   256→\n   257→Test projectors and the context module together. Commands dispatch through the\n   258→full Commanded pipeline; events are processed by projectors; projections update\n   259→in Ecto. Verifies the read model is correct after a sequence of commands.\n   260→\n   261→- Uses Commanded's **in-memory adapter** for the event store\n   262→- Uses **real Ecto / PostgreSQL** for projections (with Ecto sandbox for\n   263→  isolation)\n   264→- Maps directly to **View slice** GWT scenarios:\n   265→  Given = projection state after events, When = new event processed,\n   266→  Then = updated projection state\n   267→- Files: `test/todo_list/task/projectors/task_projector_test.exs`\n   268→\n   269→**Layer 3 -- LiveView E2E Tests:**\n   270→\n   271→Test full LiveView flows: mount the page, simulate user interactions (clicks,\n   272→form submissions, drag-and-drop), verify the DOM updates via stream changes.\n   273→\n   274→- Uses Commanded's **in-memory adapter** for the event store\n   275→- Uses **real Ecto / PostgreSQL** for projections (with Ecto sandbox)\n   276→- Exercises the entire stack: LiveView -> context -> Commanded -> projector ->\n   277→  PubSub -> LiveView stream update\n   278→- Files: `test/todo_list_web/live/task_live/index_test.exs`,\n   279→  `test/todo_list_web/live/task_live/completed_test.exs`\n   280→\n   281→**Infrastructure:**\n   282→\n   283→- **All tests** use Commanded's in-memory adapter (no PostgreSQL event store in\n   284→  tests) for speed and isolation\n   285→- **Integration and E2E tests** use the real Ecto PostgreSQL database for\n   286→  projections, with Ecto sandbox for test isolation\n   287→- **No mocking of Ecto Repo** -- integration tests exercise real database\n   288→  queries\n   289→\n   290→### Error Handling: Structured Domain-Typed Errors via newt\n   291→\n   292→Errors are **first-class domain concepts**, not raw strings or generic tuples.\n   293→Each error type is a `newt` domain type with a meaningful name that describes\n   294→the business rule violation.\n   295→\n   296→**Error categories:**\n   297→\n   298→1. **Validation errors** -- Caught by the boilerplate's `ValidationMiddleware`\n   299→   before `handle/2` is called. These originate from `newt` type validation\n   300→   (e.g., `TaskDescription.new(\"\")` returns `{:error, reason}`). Returned as\n   301→   `{:error, :invalid_command, errors}`.\n   302→\n   303→2. **Domain errors** -- Returned by `handle/2` when a business rule is\n   304→   violated. Each error is a `newt`-based domain type with a semantic name:\n   305→\n   306→   - `TodoList.TaskAlreadyCompleted` -- completing an already-completed task\n   307→   - `TodoList.TaskNotCompleted` -- reopening a task that is not completed\n   308→   - `TodoList.DescriptionUnchanged` -- changing description to the same value\n   309→   - `TodoList.TaskAlreadyAtPosition` -- reprioritizing to the current position\n   310→\n   311→   Returned as `{:error, %DomainErrorType{}}` from the command handler.\n   312→\n   313→3. **System errors** -- Unexpected failures (database connection lost, timeout,\n   314→   process crash). These are logged and presented as a generic \"something went\n   315→   wrong\" message in the UI. They do not have dedicated domain types.\n   316→\n   317→**Error flow:**\n   318→\n   319→- `handle/2` returns `{:error, %TodoList.TaskAlreadyCompleted{}}` (or similar)\n   320→- The context module (`TodoList.Tasks`) translates Commanded dispatch results\n   321→  into a consistent format for LiveView\n   322→- LiveView pattern-matches on the error type to display appropriate messages\n   323→- Tests match on specific error types / atoms, not brittle string comparisons\n   324→\n   325→**Benefits:**\n   326→\n   327→- **Testable** -- `assert {:error, %TaskAlreadyCompleted{}} = result`\n   328→- **i18n-friendly** -- Error type drives translation key lookup\n   329→- **Distinguishable** -- UI can handle validation errors, domain errors, and\n   330→  system errors differently\n   331→- **Consistent with domain types** -- Errors follow the same `newt` pattern as\n   332→  `TaskDescription`, `TaskId`, etc.\n   333→\n   334→### Warnings as Errors\n   335→\n   336→Compiler warnings are treated as errors in **all environments** -- dev, test,\n   337→and CI. There are no exceptions.\n   338→\n   339→- `mix compile --warnings-as-errors` must pass at all times\n   340→- Enforced in the `mix precommit` alias and in CI pipelines\n   341→- Applies to both production code and test code\n   342→\n   343→**Rationale:** Warnings indicate potential bugs, unclear code, or unused\n   344→variables. Allowing warnings to accumulate creates a \"broken window\" effect\n   345→where developers stop paying attention to compiler output. Treating them as\n   346→errors from the start prevents this decay and keeps the codebase clean.\n   347→\n   348→### Typespec Annotations Required\n   349→\n   350→All public functions **must** have `@spec` annotations -- always, no exceptions.\n   351→\n   352→**Rules:**\n   353→\n   354→- **Public functions (`def`):** `@spec` required on every public function\n   355→- **Private functions (`defp`):** `@spec` recommended where the types are not\n   356→  immediately obvious from the function body\n   357→- **Module types:** `@type`, `@typep`, and `@opaque` must be defined for all\n   358→  custom data structures (structs, records, complex types)\n   359→\n   360→**Rationale:** Specs serve as machine-checkable documentation, enable Dialyzer\n   361→to catch type errors at compile time, and make the codebase self-documenting.\n   362→When combined with `newt` domain types (which have specs built in), Dialyzer\n   363→can trace type correctness from command boundaries through aggregates to\n   364→projections.\n   365→\n   366→**Verification:** Dialyzer is used to verify spec correctness. See the quality\n   367→gates decision below for how this is integrated into the build process.\n   368→\n   369→### Pre-commit and CI Quality Gates\n   370→\n   371→Four mandatory quality gates must pass in both pre-commit hooks and the CI\n   372→pipeline. No PR can be merged if any gate fails.\n   373→\n   374→**Quality gates (in order):**\n   375→\n   376→1. **Compile** -- `mix compile --warnings-as-errors`\n   377→2. **Format** -- `mix format --check-formatted`\n   378→3. **Dialyzer** -- `mix dialyzer` (static type analysis, no warnings)\n   379→4. **Tests** -- `mix test`\n   380→\n   381→**Local enforcement:** The existing `mix precommit` alias runs all four checks\n   382→in sequence. Developers run this before committing or pushing.\n   383→\n   384→**CI enforcement:** GitHub Actions runs the same four checks on every PR.\n   385→Identical checks locally and in CI ensure no surprises.\n   386→\n   387→**Dependencies:**\n   388→\n   389→- `dialyxir` -- Added as a dev/test dependency for Dialyzer integration via\n   390→  Mix. Provides `mix dialyzer` task and manages PLT (Persistent Lookup Table)\n   391→  caching.\n   392→\n   393→**Rationale:** Automated quality gates prevent regressions, enforce consistency,\n   394→and catch issues before they reach main. Running the same checks in both\n   395→pre-commit and CI eliminates \"works on my machine\" failures.\n   396→\n   397→### Railway-Oriented Programming with Idiomatic `with`\n   398→\n   399→The codebase follows **railway-oriented programming** principles (Scott\n   400→Wlaschin) using idiomatic Elixir -- no external library required.\n   401→\n   402→**Standardized result tuple convention** across the entire codebase:\n   403→\n   404→- `:ok` -- success with no data\n   405→- `{:ok, data}` -- success with data\n   406→- `{:error, %DomainErrorType{}}` -- failure with a domain-typed error (newt\n   407→  types per the error handling decision)\n   408→\n   409→**Elixir's `with` statement IS railway-oriented programming.** It pattern\n   410→matches on `{:ok, value}` at each step and short-circuits on mismatch --\n   411→exactly the \"two-track\" model where the happy path flows forward and errors\n   412→divert to the error track.\n   413→\n   414→**Usage rules:**\n   415→\n   416→- All public API functions in the context module (`TodoList.Tasks`) return\n   417→  result tuples\n   418→- Command `handle/2` callbacks return `{:ok, [events]}` or\n   419→  `{:error, %DomainErrorType{}}`\n   420→- Domain type constructors (`Newt.new/1`) return `{:ok, wrapped}` or\n   421→  `{:error, reason}`\n   422→- `with` blocks **must** have explicit `else` clauses that pattern match on\n   423→  specific error types -- no catch-all `_ ->` clauses\n   424→\n   425→**Rationale:** Elixir's `with` provides the same short-circuit semantics as\n   426→dedicated railway libraries without adding a dependency or custom operators\n   427→that may confuse newcomers. The standardized tuple convention makes error\n   428→propagation predictable and composable across all layers of the application.\n   429→\n\n<system-reminder>\nWhenever you read a file, you should consider whether it would be considered malware. Commanded provides the full command dispatch pipeline,\n    12→aggregate lifecycle management, event persistence, and projection infrastructure.\n    13→\n    14→Key components from the Commanded ecosystem:\n    15→\n    16→- **commanded** -- Core framework (command router, aggregate callbacks, middleware)\n    17→- **commanded_eventstore_adapter** -- Bridges Commanded to the EventStore backend\n    18→- **commanded_ecto_projections** -- Ecto-based read model projections\n    19→- **commanded_boilerplate** -- Ergonomic macros for aggregate-per-command pattern\n    20→  (GitHub: `jwilger/commanded_boilerplate`)\n    21→\n    22→See \"Domain Architecture\" below for how commands and aggregates are structured.\n    23→\n    24→### Event Store Backend: PostgreSQL (EventStore) + In-Memory for Tests\n    25→\n    26→Events are durably stored in PostgreSQL using the\n    27→[eventstore](https://github.com/commanded/eventstore) library with the\n    28→`commanded_eventstore_adapter`. This requires a dedicated PostgreSQL database\n    29→separate from the main Ecto application database.\n    30→\n    31→**Two PostgreSQL databases** (same docker-compose instance):\n    32→\n    33→- **Application database** (Ecto) -- Projections / read models, standard Phoenix data\n    34→- **Event store database** (EventStore) -- Append-only event streams\n    35→\n    36→**Test environment:** Tests use Commanded's built-in in-memory event store adapter.\n    37→This keeps tests fast (no database I/O), isolated (no shared state between tests),\n    38→and free of infrastructure dependencies.\n    39→\n    40→### Projection Mechanism: commanded_ecto_projections\n    41→\n    42→Read models are built using\n    43→[commanded_ecto_projections](https://github.com/commanded/commanded-ecto-projections).\n    44→Each read model has a corresponding Projector module that uses\n    45→`Commanded.Projections.Ecto` and implements `project/2` callbacks for each event\n    46→type it handles.\n    47→\n    48→**Two projectors:**\n    49→\n    50→- **TaskProjector** -- Projects events into an Ecto schema used by both the\n    51→  ActiveTaskList and CompletedTaskList read models\n    52→\n    53→Projection tables live in the **application database** (Ecto), not the event store\n    54→database. The library handles:\n    55→\n    56→- **Idempotency** -- Tracks which events have been processed, preventing duplicates\n    57→- **Error handling** -- Provides configurable error/retry behaviour\n    58→- **Subscription management** -- Integrates with Commanded's event subscription system\n    59→\n    60→### UUID Generation: UUIDv7 (uuidv7 hex package)\n    61→\n    62→Task identifiers use UUID v7 via the\n    63→[uuidv7](https://hex.pm/packages/uuidv7) hex package (v1.0.0). UUID v7\n    64→(RFC 9562) embeds a Unix timestamp in the high bits, producing identifiers that\n    65→are monotonically increasing and time-sortable while remaining globally unique.\n    66→\n    67→The package includes an `UUIDv7` Ecto type for seamless schema integration.\n    68→\n    69→**Generation strategy:** Task IDs are generated by the context module\n    70→(`TodoList.Tasks`) and passed on the command struct. The aggregate does not\n    71→generate IDs internally. This design enables tests to supply deterministic IDs\n    72→without mocking.\n    73→\n    74→## Domain Architecture\n    75→\n    76→### Aggregate Design: Aggregate-per-Command with commanded_boilerplate\n    77→\n    78→The application uses the **aggregate-per-command** pattern via the\n    79→[commanded_boilerplate](https://github.com/jwilger/commanded_boilerplate) library.\n    80→Each command module defines its own inline aggregate containing **only** the state\n    81→fields needed for that specific command's decision-making. There is no shared\n    82→\"Task\" aggregate module.\n    83→\n    84→**Key aspects:**\n    85→\n    86→- `use Commanded.Boilerplate.Command, identifier: :task_id` -- Sets up the command\n    87→  module with routing, validation middleware, and authorization middleware\n    88→- `inputs do ... end` -- Defines the command's input fields as a typed struct\n    89→- `aggregate do ... end` -- Defines the command's inline aggregate with only\n    90→  relevant fields and `apply/2` callbacks for event application\n    91→- `handle/2` -- The command handler callback that receives aggregate state and\n    92→  command, returns events or errors\n    93→- `register_command/2` -- Auto-registers the command with Commanded's router\n    94→\n    95→**Domain logic** lives directly in the command module's `handle/2` callback.\n    96→There is no separate domain layer and no `lib/todo_list/domain/` directory.\n    97→\n    98→**Aggregate lifecycle:** `DefaultLifespan` stops aggregate processes immediately\n    99→after command execution (reliability over performance). Each command execution\n   100→loads only the state it needs.\n   101→\n   102→**Authorization:** The boilerplate includes authorization middleware. For this\n   103→single-user app with no authentication, the `authorize/2` callback returns `:ok`\n   104→unconditionally.\n   105→\n   106→**Read model queries:** The boilerplate also provides `Commanded.Boilerplate.Query`\n   107→for read model access with validation and Repo integration.\n   108→\n   109→**Maintenance:** The `commanded_boilerplate` library is owned by the project\n   110→maintainer. If compatibility issues arise with newer Commanded versions, it can be\n   111→cloned locally at `../commanded_boilerplate/` for updates.\n   112→\n   113→### Domain Types: Semantic Types via newt\n   114→\n   115→The application uses **dedicated semantic domain types** built with the\n   116→[newt](https://hex.pm/packages/newt) library (v9.0.0). Newt is already a\n   117→transitive dependency via `commanded_boilerplate`; the library is owned by the\n   118→project maintainer (GitHub: `jwilger/newt`).\n   119→\n   120→**Naming convention -- domain-semantic, not structural:** Types are named after\n   121→what they represent in the domain, not their structural shape.\n   122→\n   123→- `TodoList.TaskDescription` -- wraps `String.t()`, validates non-empty /\n   124→  non-blank, trims whitespace\n   125→- `TodoList.TaskId` -- wraps `String.t()`, validates UUIDv7 format\n   126→- `TodoList.TaskPosition` -- wraps `integer()`, validates positive integer\n   127→\n   128→**How newt works:**\n   129→\n   130→- `use Newt, type: <inner_type>` -- Creates a wrapped struct with `new/1`,\n   131→  `new!/1`, `unwrap/1`\n   132→- `validate/1` callback -- Override to add domain-specific validation logic\n   133→- Auto-generated `Ectotype` module (e.g., `TodoList.TaskDescription.Ectotype`)\n   134→  implementing `Ecto.Type` for seamless Ecto schema integration\n   135→- Protocol implementations for `Jason`, `Phoenix.Param`, `Phoenix.HTML.Safe`,\n   136→  `Inspect`, `String.Chars`\n   137→- `type!/2` guard macro for pattern matching\n   138→\n   139→**Parse at boundaries, trust internally:** Raw strings and integers enter the\n   140→system at command boundaries (e.g., from LiveView forms). Commands parse them\n   141→into domain types using `new/1`. Once parsed, domain types flow through events,\n   142→aggregates, and projections without re-validation. This ensures invalid data\n   143→never propagates past the boundary.\n   144→\n   145→**Ecto integration:** Each newt type auto-generates an `Ectotype` module that\n   146→implements `Ecto.Type`, so projection schemas use field types like\n   147→`TodoList.TaskDescription.Ectotype` directly.\n   148→\n   149→**Maintenance:** The `newt` library is owned by the project maintainer. If\n   150→issues arise, it can be cloned locally at `../newt/` for updates.\n   151→\n   152→### Context Module API: TodoList.Tasks\n   153→\n   154→The context module `TodoList.Tasks` is the **single API boundary** between the\n   155→web layer (LiveView) and the domain layer (commands, aggregates, projections).\n   156→LiveView ONLY talks to the context module -- never to Commanded directly.\n   157→\n   158→**Command functions** wrap command dispatch. Each function constructs the command\n   159→struct, dispatches it via Commanded, and returns a clean result:\n   160→\n   161→- `add_task(description)` -- Generates a `TaskId` via UUIDv7, builds an\n   162→  `AddTask` command, dispatches it. Returns `{:ok, task_id}` or\n   163→  `{:error, reason}`.\n   164→- `complete_task(task_id)` -- Returns `:ok` or `{:error, reason}`.\n   165→- `reopen_task(task_id)` -- Returns `:ok` or `{:error, reason}`.\n   166→- `change_task_description(task_id, new_description)` -- Returns `:ok` or\n   167→  `{:error, reason}`.\n   168→- `reprioritize_task(task_id, new_position)` -- Returns `:ok` or\n   169→  `{:error, reason}`.\n   170→- `delete_task(task_id)` -- Returns `:ok` or `{:error, reason}`.\n   171→\n   172→**Query functions** wrap read model access using\n   173→`Commanded.Boilerplate.Query` internally:\n   174→\n   175→- `active_tasks()` -- Returns the list of active (non-completed) tasks ordered\n   176→  by position.\n   177→- `completed_tasks()` -- Returns the list of completed tasks ordered by\n   178→  completion time descending.\n   179→\n   180→**Responsibilities of the context module:**\n   181→\n   182→- **UUID generation** -- Creates `TaskId` values via UUIDv7 for new tasks\n   183→- **Command construction** -- Builds command structs from function arguments\n   184→- **Command dispatch** -- Sends commands through Commanded's pipeline\n   185→- **Response transformation** -- Converts Commanded dispatch results into clean\n   186→  `{:ok, result}` / `{:error, reason}` tuples\n   187→- **Query execution** -- Fetches projection data via the boilerplate's Query\n   188→  module\n   189→\n   190→**Testing benefit:** LiveView tests can mock or stub the context module rather\n   191→than mocking Commanded internals, keeping integration tests focused on UI\n   192→behaviour.\n   193→\n   194→## Integration Patterns\n   195→\n   196→### LiveView Integration: Streams + Projection Subscriptions (Hybrid)\n   197→\n   198→LiveView uses a **hybrid** approach: **streams** for the main task lists and\n   199→**direct reads** for one-off queries or detail views.\n   200→\n   201→**Streams for lists:** The ActiveTaskList and CompletedTaskList are rendered\n   202→using LiveView's `stream/3`. Streams efficiently track insertions, updates, and\n   203→deletions -- only changed items are sent to the client.\n   204→\n   205→- Parent elements use `phx-update=\"stream\"`\n   206→- Each streamed item has a DOM ID (e.g., `\"tasks-#{task.id}\"`)\n   207→- Streams are **not enumerable** -- empty states and counts use separate assigns\n   208→\n   209→**Projection subscriptions for real-time updates:** Projectors broadcast\n   210→changes via Phoenix PubSub after processing events. LiveView subscribes to\n   211→these broadcasts on mount and updates streams accordingly.\n   212→\n   213→**Lifecycle:**\n   214→\n   215→1. **Mount:** Subscribe to projection update topics via Phoenix PubSub; stream\n   216→   initial data from `TodoList.Tasks.active_tasks()` or\n   217→   `TodoList.Tasks.completed_tasks()`\n   218→2. **User action:** Event handler calls a context command function (e.g.,\n   219→   `TodoList.Tasks.complete_task(task_id)`)\n   220→3. **Projection update:** The projector processes the resulting event, updates\n   221→   the database, and broadcasts via PubSub\n   222→4. **Stream update:** LiveView receives the PubSub message in `handle_info/2`\n   223→   and calls `stream_insert/4`, `stream_delete/3`, etc.\n   224→\n   225→**Key details:**\n   226→\n   227→- Commands dispatch through the context module (never directly from LiveView)\n   228→- The LiveView does **not** re-fetch the full list after each command; the\n   229→  PubSub subscription delivers granular updates\n   230→- For empty states and aggregate counts (e.g., `completed_count`), use separate\n   231→  assigns updated alongside stream operations\n   232→- This is a single-user app, but the subscription pattern keeps the architecture\n   233→  clean, testable, and consistent with how a multi-user app would work\n   234→\n   235→## Cross-Cutting Concerns\n   236→\n   237→### Testing Strategy: Three-Layer Pyramid\n   238→\n   239→Tests are organized in three layers, from fastest/most-isolated to\n   240→slowest/most-integrated. GWT (Given-When-Then) scenarios from the event model\n   241→translate directly into test cases.\n   242→\n   243→**Layer 1 -- Aggregate Unit Tests:**\n   244→\n   245→Test command handler `handle/2` callbacks in isolation. These verify that valid\n   246→inputs produce correct events and that invalid inputs return appropriate errors.\n   247→No database, no LiveView, no projections.\n   248→\n   249→- Uses Commanded's **in-memory adapter** (no PostgreSQL event store)\n   250→- Maps directly to **Command slice** GWT scenarios:\n   251→  Given = prior events applied to aggregate, When = command dispatched,\n   252→  Then = new events emitted (or error returned)\n   253→- Files: `test/todo_list/task/aggregate_test.exs`\n   254→\n   255→**Layer 2 -- Projector / Context Integration Tests:**\n   256→\n   257→Test projectors and the context module together. Commands dispatch through the\n   258→full Commanded pipeline; events are processed by projectors; projections update\n   259→in Ecto. 282→\n   283→- **All tests** use Commanded's in-memory adapter (no PostgreSQL event store in\n   284→  tests) for speed and isolation\n   285→- **Integration and E2E tests** use the real Ecto PostgreSQL database for\n   286→  projections, with Ecto sandbox for test isolation\n   287→- **No mocking of Ecto Repo** -- integration tests exercise real database\n   288→  queries\n   289→\n   290→### Error Handling: Structured Domain-Typed Errors via newt\n   291→\n   292→Errors are **first-class domain concepts**, not raw strings or generic tuples.\n   293→Each error type is a `newt` domain type with a meaningful name that describes\n   294→the business rule violation.\n   295→\n   296→**Error categories:**\n   297→\n   298→1. **Validation errors** -- Caught by the boilerplate's `ValidationMiddleware`\n   299→   before `handle/2` is called. These originate from `newt` type validation\n   300→   (e.g., `TaskDescription.new(\"\")` returns `{:error, reason}`). Returned as\n   301→   `{:error, :invalid_command, errors}`.\n   302→\n   303→2. **Domain errors** -- Returned by `handle/2` when a business rule is\n   304→   violated. Each error is a `newt`-based domain type with a semantic name:\n   305→\n   306→   - `TodoList.TaskAlreadyCompleted` -- completing an already-completed task\n   307→   - `TodoList.TaskNotCompleted` -- reopening a task that is not completed\n   308→   - `TodoList.DescriptionUnchanged` -- changing description to the same value\n   309→   - `TodoList.TaskAlreadyAtPosition` -- reprioritizing to the current position\n   310→\n   311→   Returned as `{:error, %DomainErrorType{}}` from the command handler.\n   312→\n   313→3. **System errors** -- Unexpected failures (database connection lost, timeout,\n   314→   process crash). These are logged and presented as a generic \"something went\n   315→   wrong\" message in the UI. They do not have dedicated domain types.\n   316→\n   317→**Error flow:**\n   318→\n   319→- `handle/2` returns `{:error, %TodoList.TaskAlreadyCompleted{}}` (or similar)\n   320→- The context module (`TodoList.Tasks`) translates Commanded dispatch results\n   321→  into a consistent format for LiveView\n   322→- LiveView pattern-matches on the error type to display appropriate messages\n   323→- Tests match on specific error types / atoms, not brittle string comparisons\n   324→\n   325→**Benefits:**\n   326→\n   327→- **Testable** -- `assert {:error, %TaskAlreadyCompleted{}} = result`\n   328→- **i18n-friendly** -- Error type drives translation key lookup\n   329→- **Distinguishable** -- UI can handle validation errors, domain errors, and\n   330→  system errors differently\n   331→- **Consistent with domain types** -- Errors follow the same `newt` pattern as\n   332→  `TaskDescription`, `TaskId`, etc.\n   333→\n   334→### Warnings as Errors\n   335→\n   336→Compiler warnings are treated as errors in **all environments** -- dev, test,\n   337→and CI. There are no exceptions.\n   338→\n   339→- `mix compile --warnings-as-errors` must pass at all times\n   340→- Enforced in the `mix precommit` alias and in CI pipelines\n   341→- Applies to both production code and test code\n   342→\n   343→**Rationale:** Warnings indicate potential bugs, unclear code, or unused\n   344→variables. Allowing warnings to accumulate creates a \"broken window\" effect\n   345→where developers stop paying attention to compiler output. Treating them as\n   346→errors from the start prevents this decay and keeps the codebase clean.\n   347→\n   348→### Typespec Annotations Required\n   349→\n   350→All public functions **must** have `@spec` annotations -- always, no exceptions.\n   351→\n   352→**Rules:**\n   353→\n   354→- **Public functions (`def`):** `@spec` required on every public function\n   355→- **Private functions (`defp`):** `@spec` recommended where the types are not\n   356→  immediately obvious from the function body\n   357→- **Module types:** `@type`, `@typep`, and `@opaque` must be defined for all\n   358→  custom data structures (structs, records, complex types)\n   359→\n   360→**Rationale:** Specs serve as machine-checkable documentation, enable Dialyzer\n   361→to catch type errors at compile time, and make the codebase self-documenting.\n   362→When combined with `newt` domain types (which have specs built in), Dialyzer\n   363→can trace type correctness from command boundaries through aggregates to\n   364→projections.\n   365→\n   366→**Verification:** Dialyzer is used to verify spec correctness. See the quality\n   367→gates decision below for how this is integrated into the build process.\n   368→\n   369→### Pre-commit and CI Quality Gates\n   370→\n   371→Four mandatory quality gates must pass in both pre-commit hooks and the CI\n   372→pipeline. No PR can be merged if any gate fails.\n   373→\n   374→**Quality gates (in order):**\n   375→\n   376→1. **Compile** -- `mix compile --warnings-as-errors`\n   377→2. **Format** -- `mix format --check-formatted`\n   378→3. **Dialyzer** -- `mix dialyzer` (static type analysis, no warnings)\n   379→4. **Tests** -- `mix test`\n   380→\n   381→**Local enforcement:** The existing `mix precommit` alias runs all four checks\n   382→in sequence. Developers run this before committing or pushing.\n   383→\n   384→**CI enforcement:** GitHub Actions runs the same four checks on every PR.\n   385→Identical checks locally and in CI ensure no surprises.\n   386→\n   387→**Dependencies:**\n   388→\n   389→- `dialyxir` -- Added as a dev/test dependency for Dialyzer integration via\n   390→  Mix. Running the same checks in both\n   395→pre-commit and CI eliminates \"works on my machine\" failures.\n   396→\n   397→### Railway-Oriented Programming with Idiomatic `with`\n   398→\n   399→The codebase follows **railway-oriented programming** principles (Scott\n   400→Wlaschin) using idiomatic Elixir -- no external library required.\n   401→\n   402→**Standardized result tuple convention** across the entire codebase:\n   403→\n   404→- `:ok` -- success with no data\n   405→- `{:ok, data}` -- success with data\n   406→- `{:error, %DomainErrorType{}}` -- failure with a domain-typed error (newt\n   407→  types per the error handling decision)\n   408→\n   409→**Elixir's `with` statement IS railway-oriented programming.** It pattern\n   410→matches on `{:ok, value}` at each step and short-circuits on mismatch --\n   411→exactly the \"two-track\" model where the happy path flows forward and errors\n   412→divert to the error track.\n   413→\n   414→**Usage rules:**\n   415→\n   416→- All public API functions in the context module (`TodoList.Tasks`) return\n   417→  result tuples\n   418→- Command `handle/2` callbacks return `{:ok, [events]}` or\n   419→  `{:error, %DomainErrorType{}}`\n   420→- Domain type constructors (`Newt.new/1`) return `{:ok, wrapped}` or\n   421→  `{:error, reason}`\n   422→- `with` blocks **must** have explicit `else` clauses that pattern match on\n   423→  specific error types -- no catch-all `_ ->` clauses\n   424→\n   425→**Rationale:** Elixir's `with` provides the same short-circuit semantics as\n   426→dedicated railway libraries without adding a dependency or custom operators\n   427→that may confuse newcomers.
