Working Agreements\n    10→\n    11→### Core Principles\n    12→- **Outcomes over output**: We measure success by user problems solved, not features\n    13→  shipped. Before starting any feature, the team articulates the user problem it solves\n    14→  and how we will know it is working (success criteria).\n    15→- **MVP discipline is sacred**: Any idea beyond the defined MVP scope gets acknowledged,\n    16→  written on the Future List (`docs/future-ideas.md`), and deferred. The answer to\n    17→  \"wouldn't it be cool if...\" is \"Yes -- in v2.\" Scope expansion requires team consensus,\n    18→  and Marty will push back hard unless there is a compelling discovery that changes our\n    19→  understanding of the user problem.\n    20→- **User stories are conversations, not contracts**: User stories guide our work but are\n    21→  owned by the whole team. Anyone can propose changes to acceptance criteria with good\n    22→  reasoning.\n    23→\n    24→### Communication\n    25→- We communicate openly, directly, and respectfully.\n    26→- Every team member's perspective is valued equally -- the accessibility specialist's\n    27→  concerns carry the same weight as the lead engineer's.\n    28→- When raising a concern, propose an alternative. \"I don't like X\" is less useful than\n    29→  \"I'd prefer Y because Z.\"\n    30→- We ask questions rather than make assumptions -- especially across disciplines.\n    31→\n    32→### Driver-Reviewer Mob Model\n    33→- **Full 9-person mob is always active.** All team members participate in every task.\n    34→- **One Driver, eight Reviewers**: The Driver is the sole agent who may modify files\n    35→  (using Edit, Write, and Bash tools). All other agents operate as Reviewers -- they\n    36→  read code, review changes, and communicate feedback via messages only.\n    37→- **Non-driver agents MUST NOT use Edit, Write, or Bash tools that modify files.**\n    38→  Violation is treated as a process failure.\n    39→- **Driver rotates by task**: The Driver is chosen based on the expertise needed for\n    40→  each task. The coordinator designates the Driver when assigning work.\n    41→- **Reviewers focus on their specialty**: Each Reviewer contributes from their area of\n    42→  expertise (a11y, UX, design, domain modeling, Rust patterns, HTMX, CSS, product,\n    43→  TDD discipline) and sends suggestions to the Driver via messages.\n    44→- **All suggestions flow through messages**: Reviewers describe intent and concerns,\n    45→  not keystrokes. The Driver translates feedback into code changes.\n    46→- **Everyone participates**: Designers, PM, accessibility specialist, domain architect --\n    47→  every perspective matters. Different eyes catch different things.\n    48→- **It's okay to say \"I don't understand.\"** The mob is a learning environment.\n    49→\n    50→### Driver Handoff Protocol\n    51→When a Driver is respawned (due to context loss, rotation, or session restart):\n    52→1. The coordinator provides a written summary of: what has been completed, what\n    53→   remains, and where to find the relevant code.\n    54→2. The new Driver reads the summary AND runs `git log --oneline -10` and\n    55→   `git diff HEAD` before writing any code.\n    56→3. The new Driver runs the full pipeline (fmt + clippy + test + playwright) to\n    57→   verify the current state is green before making changes.\n    58→4. The new Driver sends a \"ready\" message to the coordinator confirming they have\n    59→   context and a green baseline.\n    60→\n    61→### Reviewer Coordination\n    62→- Before writing a detailed review, check if other reviewers have already flagged\n    63→  the same files. Build on their observations rather than duplicating. A brief \"+1\"\n    64→  is fine for agreement.\n    65→- Once a review is acknowledged, do not re-send it.\n    66→\n    67→### Feature Workflow\n    68→Each feature follows this process with the full 9-person mob:\n    69→\n    70→1. **Discovery**: Who is the user? What is the problem? What does \"working\"\n    71→   look like? Identify edge cases (empty state, error state, 1000 items, special\n    72→   characters). Marty leads.\n    73→2. **Type sketch**: What domain types and states are involved? Quick sketch of\n    74→   enums, newtypes, and workflows. Scott leads.\n    75→3. **Design intent**: What is the visual hierarchy? What states need designing\n    76→   (empty, loading, error, success)? Steve Schoger describes layout, spacing, and\n    77→   typography in concrete terms.\n    78→4. **TDD cycle**: Red-Green-Refactor. The compiler is our first test. Take the smallest\n    79→   step possible. The Driver writes code; Reviewers provide feedback via messages.\n    80→   Kent facilitates TDD discipline.\n    81→5. **Continuous review**: Reviewers actively review each change as it happens --\n    82→   accessibility checked by Heydon, usability checked by Steve Krug, design checked\n    83→   by Steve Schoger, hypermedia patterns checked by Carson, domain modeling checked\n    84→   by Scott, Rust patterns checked by Luca, product fit checked by Marty.\n    85→6. **Consensus gate**: After each atomic green step, all 9 agents confirm the change\n    86→   is correct before the Driver proceeds to the next step. The coordinator collects\n    87→   consensus before marking any task complete.\n    88→\n    89→### Decision Cadence\n    90→- Day-to-day coding decisions (naming, small refactors, local patterns) are made\n    91→  naturally in the mob -- no formal process needed.\n    92→- Significant decisions (architecture, patterns, library choices, UX patterns, design\n    93→  system changes) use the consensus protocol defined in Section 4.\n    94→\n    95→---\n    96→\n    97→## 2. Definition of Done\n    98→\n    99→A feature is **done** when ALL of the following are true:\n   100→\n   101→### Product\n   102→- [ ] The user problem is clearly solved\n   103→- [ ] All acceptance criteria from the user story are met\n   104→- [ ] A first-time user can accomplish the task without hesitating (Trunk Test)\n   105→- [ ] User can complete a full journey from the landing page through the feature\n   106→      being delivered\n   107→- [ ] All navigation paths lead somewhere useful (no dead-end pages)\n   108→- [ ] Edge cases are handled gracefully (not just the happy path)\n   109→- [ ] The feature is deployable -- not just merged, but shippable to real users\n   110→\n   111→### Engineering\n   112→- [ ] Tests are written first (TDD: Red-Green-Refactor) and all pass\n   113→- [ ] `cargo fmt --check` passes\n   114→- [ ] `cargo clippy -- -D warnings` passes with zero warnings\n   115→- [ ] `cargo test` passes (unit + integration)\n   116→- [ ] `npx playwright test` passes -- browser-based e2e tests pass for affected\n   117→      user flows\n   118→- [ ] Error cases return meaningful HTML responses with structured logging\n   119→- [ ] Tracing spans cover the new functionality\n   120→- [ ] Database migrations (if any) are committed and `sqlx-data.json` is updated\n   121→\n   122→### Accessibility (WCAG 2.2 AA)\n   123→- [ ] HTML is semantic and uses correct elements (`<button>`, `<label>`, `<ul>`, etc.)\n   124→- [ ] All form inputs have visible `<label>` elements (no placeholder-only inputs)\n   125→- [ ] All interactive elements are fully keyboard operable\n   126→- [ ] All interactive elements have unique accessible names including the item they\n   127→      act on (e.g., \"Delete: Buy groceries\", not just \"Delete\")\n   128→- [ ] Structural a11y verified via axe-core. Manual screen reader testing (VoiceOver,\n   129→      NVDA, or equivalent) for NEW interaction patterns (modals, live regions, focus\n   130→      management). Routine pages covered by axe-core don't require manual SR testing\n   131→      on every change\n   132→- [ ] ARIA used only when native HTML semantics are insufficient (with comments explaining why)\n   133→- [ ] Color contrast meets WCAG AA (4.5:1 for normal text, 3:1 for large text/UI)\n   134→- [ ] Color is never the only indicator of state (always a secondary visual cue)\n   135→- [ ] Focus management is correct after HTMX swaps (see HTMX Focus Protocol below)\n   136→- [ ] Custom `:focus-visible` styles are present with sufficient contrast\n   137→- [ ] `prefers-reduced-motion` is respected for all animations/transitions\n   138→\n   139→### Design\n   140→- [ ] Visual design follows the established design token system\n   141→- [ ] All states are designed: empty, loading, error, success\n   142→- [ ] Visual hierarchy is clear -- one primary focal point per screen\n   143→- [ ] Spacing is consistent and uses the defined scale\n   144→\n   145→### Frontend\n   146→- [ ] Core functionality works via standard HTML forms and links (progressive\n   147→      enhancement -- HTMX and TypeScript enhance but are not required for basic operation)\n   148→- [ ] HTMX attributes follow locality of behavior (self-describing elements)\n   149→- [ ] TypeScript (if any) is non-critical and has accessible alternatives\n   150→\n   151→### Process\n   152→- [ ] The mob has continuously reviewed code, design, usability, and accessibility\n   153→      during development\n   154→- [ ] All 9 team members have reviewed and consent to the completed work\n   155→- [ ] Labels and copy follow the Copy Standards (see Section 3)\n   156→- [ ] Progress markers updated in `docs/gtd-product-discovery.md` Implementation Order\n   157→      (mark step `[x]`, move `<!-- NEXT -->` marker, update \"Current step\" summary)\n   158→\n   159→---\n   160→\n   161→## 3. Code Conventions and Patterns\n   162→\n   163→### Project Structure\n   164→\n   165→```\n   166→src/\n   167→  main.rs              -- Startup, configuration loading, server binding\n   168→  lib.rs               -- Re-exports for integration test access\n   169→  configuration.rs     -- Config structs, environment-aware loading\n   170→  startup.rs           -- Application builder (Router, DB pool, middleware)\n   171→  routes/              -- HTTP handlers (thin: extract, delegate, respond)\n   172→    mod.rs\n   173→    health_check.rs\n   174→  domain/              -- Pure domain types and logic (NO I/O)\n   175→    mod.rs\n   176→  services/            -- Application services (orchestrate domain + infra)\n   177→    mod.rs\n   178→  infrastructure/      -- Database queries, external service clients\n   179→    mod.rs\n   180→  templates/           -- Askama HTML templates\n   181→tests/\n   182→  api/                 -- Integration tests against the full HTTP stack\n   183→    mod.rs\n   184→    helpers.rs         -- TestApp, spawn_app(), shared fixtures\n   185→    health_check.rs\n   186→```\n   187→\n   188→Dependencies flow inward: routes -> services -> domain + infrastructure.\n   189→Domain depends on nothing. This makes the domain layer trivially testable.\n   190→\n   191→### Rust Conventions\n   192→\n   193→**Type-driven domain modeling:**\n   194→- Newtypes for all domain identifiers and constrained values: `UserId(Uuid)`,\n   195→  `Email(String)`, `Title(String)`, `TodoItemId(Uuid)`\n   196→- Enums for state machines -- make illegal states unrepresentable:\n   197→  ```rust\n   198→  // GOOD: the type system prevents invalid states\n   199→  enum TodoItem {\n   200→      Pending { title: Title, created_at: DateTime<Utc> },\n   201→      Completed { title: Title, created_at: DateTime<Utc>, completed_at: DateTime<Utc> },\n   202→  }\n   203→  ```\n   204→- **Parse, don't validate**: Instead of `fn validate(input: &str) -> bool`, write\n   205→  `fn parse(input: String) -> Result<Email, ValidationError>`. Validation that returns\n   206→  a boolean throws away information. Parsing produces a typed value that carries the\n   207→  proof of validity. Validate once at the boundary; never re-validate inside the system.\n   208→\n   209→**Workflows as type-safe pipelines:**\n   210→```\n   211→UnvalidatedInput -> ValidatedInput -> DomainEvent -> PersistenceResult\n   212→```\n   213→Each step's output type is the next step's input. You cannot skip validation or\n   214→persist before validating.\n   215→\n   216→**Error handling (three layers):**\n   217→- **Domain errors**: Custom enum with `thiserror`. Domain terms only -- no HTTP concepts,\n   218→  no infrastructure types. A `TodoError::TitleEmpty` must never contain a `sqlx::Error`.\n   219→  Domain errors and infrastructure errors are separate types, translated at the boundary.\n   220→  ```rust\n   221→  #[derive(Debug, thiserror::Error)]\n   222→  pub enum TodoError {\n   223→      #[error(\"Todo title cannot be empty\")]\n   224→      TitleEmpty,\n   225→      #[error(\"Todo title too long (max {max}, got {actual})\")]\n   226→      TitleTooLong { max: usize, actual: usize },\n   227→      #[error(\"Todo not found\")]\n   228→      NotFound { id: TodoItemId },\n   229→      #[error(transparent)]\n   230→      Unexpected(#[from] anyhow::Error),\n   231→  }\n   232→  ```\n   233→- **Service errors**: Map domain errors to actionable responses. Add context.\n   234→- **Route errors**: Implement `IntoResponse` for error types. Return meaningful HTML\n   235→  (not raw 500s). Every error path produces a user-facing response.\n   236→- **Always add context** when propagating errors. A bare `?` that loses context is a\n   237→  code smell.\n   238→- **Log at error boundaries**: Every error crossing an architectural boundary gets\n   239→  logged with structured `tracing` fields.\n   240→\n   241→**Idiomatic Rust:**\n   242→- Prefer iterators over loops, pattern matching over conditionals\n   243→- `?` operator for error propagation with context\n   244→- `#[must_use]` on important return types\n   245→- Compile-time guarantees: SQLx `query!`/`query_as!` macros, Askama templates\n   246→\n   247→**Testing strategy (TDD):**\n   248→- **Unit tests** (`#[cfg(test)] mod tests`): Pure domain logic, validation, type\n   249→  conversions. Fast, no I/O, no mocking. **Litmus test: if you need a mock to test\n   250→  domain logic, I/O has leaked into the domain layer. Push it back to the boundary.**\n   251→- **Integration tests** (`tests/` directory): Full HTTP stack with real database.\n   252→  `TestApp` struct with `spawn_app()` helper. Unique database per test run\n   253→  (random name, run migrations, drop after).\n   254→- **No mocks for the database**: Use real PostgreSQL via Docker. Mocks give false\n   255→  confidence.\n   256→- **Test names as behavior specifications**:\n   257→  ```rust\n   258→  #[tokio::test]\n   259→  async fn registration_returns_422_when_email_is_missing() { ... }\n   260→  ```\n   261→- **Acceptance tests as usability statements**: \"When I type a todo and press Enter,\n   262→  it appears in my list.\" Tests describe what the user expects to happen.\n   263→- **Property-based tests** with `proptest` where appropriate.\n   264→- **End-to-end tests** (`e2e/` directory): Playwright browser tests against the\n   265→  running application. Cover critical user journeys (register, login, core feature,\n   266→  logout). Use role-based and label-based locators (`getByRole`, `getByLabel`) so\n   267→  tests double as accessibility assertions. Keep this layer thin -- only add e2e\n   268→  tests for flows that integration tests cannot adequately verify.\n   269→- **Accessibility testing** (four layers):\n   270→  - *Automated*: axe-core (or equivalent) in the test suite for missing labels,\n   271→    contrast violations, and structural issues\n   272→  - *Keyboard*: Manual keyboard navigation testing for every interactive flow\n   273→  - *Screen reader*: Manual VoiceOver/NVDA testing for every feature\n   274→  - *Structural*: HTML validation for semantic correctness\n   275→  Tests can assert on roles, labels, and ARIA attributes -- documenting the expected\n   276→  screen reader experience as living specifications.\n   277→\n   278→### Initial Crate List\n   279→\n   280→Proposed starting dependencies (open to mob discussion):\n   281→\n   282→| Crate | Purpose |\n   283→|-------|---------|\n   284→| `axum` | Web framework |\n   285→| `tokio` (full features) | Async runtime |\n   286→| `sqlx` (postgres, migrate, runtime-tokio-rustls) | Database |\n   287→| `askama` + `askama_axum` | Templates |\n   288→| `serde` + `serde_json` | Serialization |\n   289→| `tracing` + `tracing-subscriber` (env-filter) | Observability |\n   290→| `thiserror` | Domain error types |\n   291→| `anyhow` | Ad-hoc error context |\n   292→| `argon2` | Password hashing |\n   293→| `tower-sessions` + `tower-sessions-sqlx-store` | Session management |\n   294→| `uuid` | Identifiers |\n   295→\n   296→Note: Input validation will be handled through custom newtypes with validation in\n   297→constructors (Scott's approach), not a validation framework. The types carry the\n   298→proof of validity.\n   299→\n   300→### HTML / HTMX Conventions\n   301→\n   302→**The Hypermedia Contract:**\n   303→- **Return HTML, not JSON.** Every UI endpoint returns HTML. No JSON API layer.\n   304→- **Semantic HTML first**: `<button>` for actions, `<a>` for navigation, `<form>` for\n   305→  data submission, `<ul>`/`<ol>` for lists. Never `<div onclick>`.\n   306→- **Form accessibility**: Every input has a visible `<label>` (never placeholder-only).\n   307→  Validation errors are associated with inputs via `aria-describedby` and announced\n   308→  via `aria-live=\"polite\"` regions. Use `aria-live=\"assertive\"` only for critical errors.\n   309→- **Locality of behavior**: Every HTMX-enhanced element is self-describing. You\n   310→  understand what it does by looking at it alone.\n   311→- **No client-side state**: The DOM is the state, the server is the source of truth.\n   312→  No client-side data stores. The only acceptable client-side state is transient UI\n   313→  state for progressive enhancement (e.g., drag position).\n   314→\n   315→**Server endpoint conventions:**\n   316→- **Full page requests** (no `HX-Request` header): Return complete HTML page with\n   317→  layout, nav, landmarks.\n   318→- **HTMX requests** (with `HX-Request` header): Return just the HTML fragment for\n   319→  the swap.\n   320→- **`HX-Trigger` response header** for cross-component updates (e.g., updating a\n   321→  todo count after deletion).\n   322→- **Same URL, same handler**: One handler checks the `HX-Request` header to decide\n   323→  whether to return a full page or a fragment. No separate `/api/` routes.\n   324→- **HTTP methods used semantically**: GET = read, POST = create, PUT/PATCH = update,\n   325→  DELETE = delete.\n   326→- **Status codes**: 200 for success with HTML, 422 for validation errors with error\n   327→  HTML, 200 with empty body for deletion (allows HTMX swap to remove element).\n   328→\n   329→**HTMX Architecture Strategy:**\n   330→- `hx-boost=\"true\"` on `<body>` — universal navigation enhancement. All `<a>` and\n   331→  `<form>` elements automatically use AJAX with history management. No per-link\n   332→  attributes needed for standard navigation.\n   333→- **Explicit attributes for in-page interactions**: Use `hx-post`, `hx-target`,\n   334→  `hx-swap` for operations that update part of the page without navigation (e.g.,\n   335→  adding a todo item, deleting an inbox item).\n   336→- **Auth forms opt out** with `hx-boost=\"false\"` — login/logout/register forms need\n   337→  full page redirects for session cookie handling.\n   338→- **Server renders full pages; boost handles swap transparently.** Handlers check the\n   339→  `HX-Request` header to decide whether to return a full page or a fragment.\n   340→\n   341→**Progressive enhancement (non-negotiable):**\n   342→- The app MUST work without JavaScript. Forms submit, links navigate, content is\n   343→  readable with HTML alone.\n   344→- HTMX enhances the experience (partial updates, no full page reloads).\n   345→- TypeScript is only for things neither HTML nor HTMX can do.\n   346→\n   347→**HTMX Focus Management Protocol:**\n   348→After every HTMX swap:\n   349→- If an element was **removed**: Move focus to the logical next element.\n   350→- If content was **updated in place**: Keep focus where it was.\n   351→- Use `aria-live=\"polite\"` regions to announce state changes to screen readers.\n   352→- Test every HTMX interaction with Tab key before considering it done.\n   353→\n   354→**Page structure (every page):**\n   355→- Skip link to main content (first focusable element)\n   356→- Landmark regions: `<main>`, `<nav>`, `<header>`, `<footer>`\n   357→- Logical heading hierarchy: one `<h1>` per page, no skipped levels\n   358→- Descriptive `<title>` element\n   359→\n   360→### CSS Conventions\n   361→\n   362→**Progressive enhancement layers:**\n   363→1. **Layer 1 (HTML)**: Functional and readable with zero CSS.\n   364→2. **Layer 2 (CSS)**: Beautiful -- layout, typography, color, transitions, focus styles.\n   365→3. **Layer 3 (TypeScript)**: Delightful -- drag-and-drop, advanced keyboard shortcuts.\n   366→\n   367→**CSS organization with cascade layers:**\n   368→```css\n   369→@layer reset, tokens, base, layout, components, utilities;\n   370→```\n   371→- **reset**: Normalize/reset styles\n   372→- **tokens**: Custom properties (design tokens)\n   373→- **base**: Element-level styles (body, headings, links, forms)\n   374→- **layout**: Page-level layout (CSS Grid)\n   375→- **components**: Component-specific styles (todo-item, auth-form)\n   376→- **utilities**: Helper classes (visually-hidden, etc.)\n   377→- No `!important` unless in the utilities layer for intentional overrides.\n   378→- CSS nesting is fine for component-scoped styles but avoid nesting deeper than\n   379→  2 levels.\n   380→\n   381→**Design tokens (CSS custom properties on `:root`):**\n   382→- **Spacing scale** (4px base): 4, 8, 12, 16, 24, 32, 48, 64, 96 -- encoded as\n   383→  `--space-xs` through `--space-3xl`\n   384→- **Color palette**: oklch color space for perceptual uniformity. One primary color,\n   385→  neutral gray palette (50-900), semantic colors (danger, success, warning). Most UI\n   386→  is grayscale; color is for emphasis and interaction.\n   387→- **Typography**: System font stack (`system-ui, sans-serif`). Type scale from xs to\n   388→  3xl with defined line-height. Tighter for headings, looser for body.\n   389→- **Shadows**: Three levels (sm, md, lg). Never combine shadows and borders on the\n   390→  same element.\n   391→- **Border radius**: Three sizes (sm, md, lg).\n   392→- **All values reference tokens -- no hardcoded hex values or pixel values in\n   393→  component styles.**\n   394→\n   395→**Design tokens are a prerequisite**: The token system (spacing, colors, typography,\n   396→shadows, radii) must be established and agreed upon before any feature UI work begins.\n   397→This is foundational -- without it, inconsistent one-off values accumulate from day one.\n   398→\n   399→**Design token governance**: Adding a new color, spacing value, or typography level\n   400→goes through the mob (Steve Schoger approves design token changes).\n   401→\n   402→**Design token flow**: Steve Schoger defines the visual design -> Lea encodes as CSS\n   403→custom properties -> Components reference only tokens -> Themes/dark mode reassign\n   404→properties. No build step. No JSON-to-CSS pipeline.\n   405→\n   406→**Modern CSS features:**\n   407→- `:has()` for parent-based styling (e.g., `li:has(input:checked)` for completed todos)\n   408→- Container queries where components need to respond to container size\n   409→- Logical properties (`margin-inline`, `padding-block`) for future RTL support\n   410→- `clamp()` for fluid typography\n   411→- View Transitions API for smooth HTMX swap animations\n   412→- `@supports` for graceful degradation of newer features\n   413→\n   414→**Accessibility in CSS:**\n   415→- Custom `:focus-visible` styles with at least 3:1 contrast. Never `outline: none`\n   416→  without a replacement.\n   417→- `prefers-reduced-motion`: All animations/transitions wrapped in a motion query.\n   418→  Reduced or no motion as the alternative.\n   419→- `prefers-color-scheme`: Supported if/when the team decides to add dark mode.\n   420→- Color is never the only state indicator.\n   421→\n   422→**Responsive design**: Mobile-first. Default styles target the smallest viewport;\n   423→enhancements added via `min-width` media queries. Breakpoints: mobile (default),\n   424→desktop (~1024px). A todo list should work beautifully on a phone.\n   425→\n   426→**Browser targets**: Last 2 versions of evergreen browsers (Chrome, Firefox, Safari,\n   427→Edge). No IE11. `@supports` for graceful degradation. No polyfills unless necessary.\n   428→\n   429→### TypeScript Conventions\n   430→- **No framework**: Vanilla TypeScript with DOM APIs.\n   431→- **Progressive enhancement pattern**: Feature works without JS, TypeScript enhances.\n   432→- **Event delegation**: Listeners on parent containers, not individual elements.\n   433→- **State via data attributes**: TypeScript toggles `data-*` attributes or classes;\n   434→  CSS handles all visual changes based on those.\n   435→- **No CSS-in-JS**: Styles live in CSS files. TypeScript never sets inline styles\n   436→  (except computed values like drag position).\n   437→- **Thin layer**: If a TypeScript file is getting large, we are probably doing\n   438→  something CSS or HTMX could handle.\n   439→\n   440→### Copy Standards\n   441→- **Labels**: 1-2 words when possible.\n   442→- **Error messages**: Plain language. Say what went wrong, suggest what to do next.\n   443→  \"That email isn't registered -- want to create an account?\" not \"Error: User not found.\"\n   444→- **Button labels**: Describe the action (\"Add todo\", \"Sign in\"), not vague labels\n   445→  (\"Submit\", \"OK\").\n   446→- **No happy talk**: Every word earns its place or gets cut. No introductory paragraphs\n   447→  that say nothing useful.\n   448→- **Design for scanning, not reading**: Users don't read pages, they scan. Clear\n   449→  headings, short text, prominent calls to action, no walls of text.\n   450→- **Cut the text, then cut it again**: If you wrote a paragraph, ask \"can I say this\n   451→  in half the words?\"\n   452→\n   453→### Domain Language and Modeling Conventions\n   454→- Code uses the ubiquitous language of the domain. \"Complete a task\" ->\n   455→  `complete_task()`, not `update_status()`.\n   456→- Domain types are explicit -- no primitive obsession. Every domain concept gets its\n   457→  own type, even if it is \"just a string\" or \"just a UUID\" underneath.\n   458→- Newtypes are constructed only through validated factory methods (the `parse`\n   459→  pattern). You cannot create a `TodoTitle` from an arbitrary string without going\n   460→  through validation.\n   461→- Every `is_*` boolean flag is a candidate for an enum. Ask: \"what states does this\n   462→  represent?\" and model them explicitly.\n   463→- Maintain a domain glossary in `docs/glossary.md` mapping business terms to types:\n   464→\n   465→  | Domain Term | Rust Type | Notes |\n   466→  |-------------|-----------|-------|\n   467→  | User | `User` | Authenticated user with valid credentials |\n   468→  | Email | `ValidatedEmail` | Constructed via `parse`, not `new` |\n   469→  | Todo item | `TodoItem` (enum) | `Pending` or `Completed` variant |\n   470→  | Todo title | `TodoTitle` | Non-empty, max length, validated at construction |\n   471→\n   472→### Observability\n   473→\n   474→**Structured logging with `tracing`:**\n   475→- Request ID (UUID) attached to every request via middleware.\n   476→- Span fields: `request_id`, `method`, `uri`, `status_code`.\n   477→- Application-level spans for significant operations: `register_user`,\n   478→  `authenticate`, `create_todo`, etc.\n   479→- Use `#[tracing::instrument]` for service functions.\n   480→- Structured fields on errors: what failed, why, relevant IDs.\n   481→\n   482→**Log level conventions:**\n   483→| Level | When to use |\n   484→|-------|-------------|\n   485→| `ERROR` | Something is broken, needs human attention |\n   486→| `WARN` | Unexpected but handled (e.g., invalid login attempt) |\n   487→| `INFO` | Significant business events (user registered, todo created) |\n   488→| `DEBUG` | Technical details useful for debugging |\n   489→| `TRACE` | Very verbose (request/response bodies, SQL queries) |\n   490→\n   491→### Database Conventions\n   492→- **Migrations**: SQLx migrations (`sqlx migrate`), numbered SQL files, version controlled.\n   493→- **Compile-time checked queries**: `sqlx::query!` and `sqlx::query_as!` macros.\n   494→- **Offline mode for CI**: `sqlx-data.json` generated via `cargo sqlx prepare`,\n   495→  committed to version control.\n   496→- **Connection pool**: `PgPool` shared via Axum state.\n   497→- **UUIDs for primary keys**: `uuid` type in PostgreSQL, `Uuid` in Rust.\n   498→- **Timestamps**: `timestamptz` in PostgreSQL, `chrono::DateTime<Utc>` or\n   499→  `time::OffsetDateTime` in Rust.\n   500→- **Naming conventions**: snake_case for tables and columns. Plural table names\n   501→  (`users`, `todos`).\n   502→\n   503→### Configuration Management\n   504→- Layered configuration: `base.yaml` (defaults) -> `local.yaml` (gitignored overrides)\n   505→  -> environment variables (12-factor style).\n   506→- **Fail fast**: Missing required configuration at startup panics with a clear message.\n   507→  No silent defaults for critical settings (database URL, secret keys).\n   508→- Separate configuration structs: `DatabaseSettings`, `ApplicationSettings`,\n   509→  `AuthSettings`.\n   510→\n   511→### CI/CD Quality Gates\n   512→\n   513→Every commit must pass (in order):\n   514→1. `cargo fmt --check`\n   515→2. `cargo clippy -- -D warnings`\n   516→3. `cargo test` (unit + integration)\n   517→4. `npx playwright test` (browser-based e2e)\n   518→5. `cargo audit` (dependency vulnerabilities)\n   519→\n   520→### Atomic Green Step Pipeline\n   521→\n   522→*Every change follows this pipeline. No shortcuts, no skipped steps.*\n   523→\n   524→1. **Write code** — the smallest meaningful change.\n   525→2. **`cargo fmt --check`** — fix formatting if needed.\n   526→3. **`cargo clippy -- -D warnings`** — fix warnings if needed.\n   527→4. **`cargo test`** — fix failures if needed.\n   528→5. **`npx playwright test`** — fix e2e failures if needed.\n   529→6. **Refactor** — look for duplication, unclear names, or structural improvements\n   530→   before committing. The Refactor step is not optional.\n   531→7. **Glossary check** — verify new domain types/fields match `docs/glossary.md`. If\n   532→   deviating, update the glossary first (with domain architect approval).\n   533→8. **`git commit`** — commit locally. **Do NOT push yet.**\n   534→9. **All 9 agents review and reach consensus** — Driver and Reviewers confirm the change\n   535→   is correct. If concerns are raised, the Driver fixes them, re-runs steps 2–7, and\n   536→   re-seeks consensus.\n   537→10. **Once 9/9 consensus → `git push`.**\n   538→11. **Wait for CI green** — run `gh run list --limit 1` and WAIT for CI to complete\n   539→    green before beginning the next change. Never have more than 1 pending CI run. If\n   540→    CI fails, fix it before pushing anything else. If CI was skipped because only\n   541→    non-code files changed (per `paths-ignore` in the workflow), treat that push as\n   542→    implicitly green and proceed.\n   543→12. **Mini-retrospective** (1-minute checkpoint) — The **team** (not the coordinator,\n   544→    not the project owner) conducts this. The Driver initiates and all 9 agents\n   545→    participate. Questions: (a) Did we follow the pipeline? (b) Was the commit\n   546→    atomic? (c) Any process improvements? The project owner may offer suggestions as\n   547→    an outside observer, but all process decisions are the team's to make.\n   548→13. **Only then begin the next change.**\n   549→\n   550→Additional rules:\n   551→- **Consensus before push.** Code is reviewed locally before it reaches the remote. This\n   552→  keeps the CI wait out of the feedback loop.\n   553→- **If CI fails, fix it before writing new code.** A red CI is the team's top priority.\n   554→  No new features, no new tests, no refactoring until CI is green again.\n   555→- **One Driver at a time.** Only the designated Driver may modify files. Non-driver agents\n   556→  MUST NOT use Edit, Write, or Bash tools that modify files. Violation is treated as a\n   557→  process failure.\n   558→\n   559→### Dependency Management\n   560→\n   561→Before adding a new crate:\n   562→- Is it well-maintained? (Recent commits, responsive maintainers)\n   563→- Is it widely used? (Downloads, reverse dependencies)\n   564→- Compatible license? (MIT/Apache-2.0 preferred)\n   565→- Can we avoid it? (Prefer stdlib or existing dependencies)\n   566→\n   567→### Documentation\n   568→- **Code comments**: Only where \"why\" is not obvious from the code.\n   569→- **ADRs**: For significant technical decisions. Format: context, decision,\n   570→  consequences. Stored in `docs/adr/`.\n   571→- **Domain glossary**: `docs/glossary.md` mapping business terms to code.\n   572→- **README**: Practical -- how to set up, run tests, run the app.\n   573→\n   574→---\n   575→\n   576→## 4. Disagreement Resolution\n   577→\n   578→### In the Mob (Day-to-Day)\n   579→1. State the disagreement clearly: \"I think X, you think Y.\"\n   580→2. Each side explains their reasoning briefly (< 2 minutes each).\n   581→3. If possible, **try both and let the code decide** -- write a quick test or prototype.\n   582→4. If one approach is simpler, prefer it (smallest viable decision).\n   583→5. If still stuck after 5 minutes, the mob votes. Majority wins for day-to-day decisions.\n   584→   The dissenter can say \"I disagree but won't block.\"\n   585→\n   586→### For Significant Decisions (Consensus Protocol)\n   587→1. Any team member raises the decision point with a proposal and reasoning.\n   588→2. Each team member shares their perspective (concerns, alternatives, support).\n   589→3. Discussion continues until:\n   590→   - **Consensus**: Everyone agrees or consents (\"I can live with this\").\n   591→   - **Compromise**: A synthesized solution addresses all concerns.\n   592→   - **Stand-aside**: \"I disagree but won't block\" -- recorded and respected.\n   593→4. If no consensus after **10 rounds** of substantive discussion, **escalate to the\n   594→   project owner** with:\n   595→   - Options considered\n   596→   - Each member's position\n   597→   - Trade-offs\n   598→   - Team recommendation (if possible)\n   599→\n   600→### When to Involve the Project Owner\n   601→- Consensus deadlock after 10 rounds\n   602→- Any proposed change to MVP scope\n   603→- Questions about target user or business context the team cannot answer\n   604→- Major architectural pivots that significantly change the timeline\n   605→- Brief status updates at milestones (keep the owner informed, don't go dark)\n   606→\n   607→### Principles\n   608→- Disagree with the idea, not the person.\n   609→- Once decided, **disagree and commit** -- no undermining, no \"I told you so.\"\n   610→- Revisit decisions when new information emerges (from tests, users, or production).\n   611→- **Write it down**: Major decisions recorded as Architecture Decision Records (ADRs)\n   612→  in `docs/adr/`.\n   613→\n   614→---\n   615→\n   616→## 5. Architectural Principles\n   617→\n   618→1. **Simplicity first**: Choose the simplest approach that could work. Add complexity\n   619→   only when tests or user feedback demand it. \"Could this be simpler?\" is always a\n   620→   valid question.\n   621→2. **Server-side state**: The server is the source of truth for both data and\n   622→   presentation. The browser renders what the server sends. No client-side state\n   623→   management.\n   624→3. **Pure domain core**: Domain logic is pure functions and types with no I/O. Side\n   625→   effects live at the boundaries. This makes the domain trivially testable.\n   626→4. **Make illegal states unrepresentable**: Use the type system to prevent bugs at\n   627→   compile time. Newtypes, enums, and validated types carry proof of correctness.\n   628→5. **Production-ready from day one**: Observability, error handling, and structured\n   629→   logging from the first line of code -- not bolted on later.\n   630→6. **Accessibility is a quality, not a feature**: Every feature is accessible from the\n   631→   moment it is built. Inaccessible is broken. ~15-20% of users have some form of\n   632→   disability -- that is not an edge case.\n   633→7. **Progressive enhancement**: HTML works -> CSS makes it beautiful -> JS makes it\n   634→   delightful. Each layer enhances without being required by the layers above.\n   635→8. **Conventions over cleverness**: Follow established patterns. A login form should\n   636→   look like every other login form. Don't make the user think. Design for scanning,\n   637→   not reading. Cut unnecessary words. When in doubt, simplify.\n   638→9. **Continuous testing**: TDD keeps us honest. The compiler is our first test. We\n   639→   never skip the red step. Tests read like behavior specifications.\n   640→10. **Incremental design**: Let the design emerge from tests and feedback. Don't\n   641→    over-design upfront. Make the code a little better before adding a feature (Tidy\n   642→    First), but don't redesign the universe. Ship early, learn fast.\n   643→11. **Walking skeleton first**: Our first milestone is the thinnest possible slice\n   644→    through the entire stack -- a user can register, log in, see an empty todo list,\n   645→    add one item, and log out. Everything else builds on top.\n   646→12. **Validate at the boundary, trust the types**: Input validation happens once, at\n   647→    the system boundary. It produces typed values that carry proof of validity.\n   648→    The interior of the system trusts its own types.\n   649→\n   650→---\n   651→\n   652→## 6. Retrospective Cadence\n   653→\n   654→All team members are AI agents operating continuously. Time-based retros (weekly,\n   655→bi-weekly) do not apply. Instead, retros are triggered by events.\n   656→\n   657→- **After each feature**: Retro immediately after completing a feature. What worked?\n   658→  What didn't? What should we change?\n   659→- **After significant incidents**: If a build breaks, a major refactor goes sideways,\n   660→  or the team gets stuck for an extended period, retro after resolution.\n   661→- **Format**: Simple Start/Stop/Continue.\n   662→- **Action items**: Every retro produces at most 2-3 concrete action items. These are\n   663→  tracked and checked at the next retro.\n   664→- **Agreements are living**: These team agreements can be updated at any retro if the\n   665→  team reaches consensus.\n   666→- **Usability testing**: Aim for informal testing -- three users, 20 minutes each --\n   667→  at natural breakpoints. Even watching one person use the app for 5 minutes reveals\n   668→  more than a week of discussion.\n   669→- **Post-CI checkpoint**: After each CI build (pass or fail), the **team** conducts\n   670→  this checkpoint — NOT the coordinator, NOT the project owner. The Driver initiates\n   671→  and all 9 agents participate: (a) Did we follow the pipeline? (b) Was the commit\n   672→  atomic? (c) Any process improvements? This is a 1-minute checkpoint, not a full\n   673→  retro. The project owner may offer suggestions as an outside observer/consultant,\n   674→  but all process decisions are the team's to make.\n   675→- **Deferred items**: Non-blocking a11y, design, and UX items are tracked in\n   676→  `docs/deferred-items.md` and reviewed at each retrospective.\n   677→\n   678→---\n   679→\n   680→## 7. Tooling & Repository\n   681→\n   682→### Source Control\n   683→- **Repository**: Public GitHub repository under the `jwilger` account\n   684→- **License**: MIT\n   685→- **Branching**: Work on `main` for now.
